<p class="line" name=speech40><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.126>Nay, it is true, or else I am a Turk:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.127>You rise to play and go to bed to work.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech41><b>EMILIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.128>You shall not write my praise.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech42><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.129>No, let me not.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech43><b>DESDEMONA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.130>What wouldst thou write of me, if thou shouldst</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.131>praise me?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech44><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.132>O gentle lady, do not put me to't;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.133>For I am nothing, if not critical.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech45><b>DESDEMONA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.134>Come on assay. There's one gone to the harbour?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech46><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.135>Ay, madam.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech47><b>DESDEMONA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.136>I am not merry; but I do beguile</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.137>The thing I am, by seeming otherwise.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.138>Come, how wouldst thou praise me?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech48><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.139>I am about it; but indeed my invention</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.140>Comes from my pate as birdlime does from frize;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.141>It plucks out brains and all: but my Muse labours,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.142>And thus she is deliver'd.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.143>If she be fair and wise, fairness and wit,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.144>The one's for use, the other useth it.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech49><b>DESDEMONA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.145>Well praised! How if she be black and witty?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech50><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.146>If she be black, and thereto have a wit,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.147>She'll find a white that shall her blackness fit.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech51><b>DESDEMONA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.148>Worse and worse.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech52><b>EMILIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.149>How if fair and foolish?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech53><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.150>She never yet was foolish that was fair;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.151>For even her folly help'd her to an heir.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech54><b>DESDEMONA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.152>These are old fond paradoxes to make fools laugh i'</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.153>the alehouse. What miserable praise hast thou for</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.154>her that's foul and foolish?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech55><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.155>There's none so foul and foolish thereunto,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.156>But does foul pranks which fair and wise ones do.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech56><b>DESDEMONA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.157>O heavy ignorance! thou praisest the worst best.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.158>But what praise couldst thou bestow on a deserving</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.159>woman indeed, one that, in the authority of her</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.160>merit, did justly put on the vouch of very malice itself?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech57><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.161>She that was ever fair and never proud,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.162>Had tongue at will and yet was never loud,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.163>Never lack'd gold and yet went never gay,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.164>Fled from her wish and yet said 'Now I may,'</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.165>She that being anger'd, her revenge being nigh,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.166>Bade her wrong stay and her displeasure fly,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.167>She that in wisdom never was so frail</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.168>To change the cod's head for the salmon's tail;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.169>She that could think and ne'er disclose her mind,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.170>See suitors following and not look behind,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.171>She was a wight, if ever such wight were,--</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech58><b>DESDEMONA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.172>To do what?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech59><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.173>To suckle fools and chronicle small beer.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech60><b>DESDEMONA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.174>O most lame and impotent conclusion! Do not learn</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.175>of him, Emilia, though he be thy husband. How say</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.176>you, Cassio? is he not a most profane and liberal</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.177>counsellor?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech61><b>CASSIO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.178>He speaks home, madam: You may relish him more in</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.179>the soldier than in the scholar.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech62><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.180>[Aside]  He takes her by the palm: ay, well said,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.181>whisper: with as little a web as this will I</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.182>ensnare as great a fly as Cassio. Ay, smile upon</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.183>her, do; I will gyve thee in thine own courtship.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.184>You say true; 'tis so, indeed: if such tricks as</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.185>these strip you out of your lieutenantry, it had</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.186>been better you had not kissed your three fingers so</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.187>oft, which now again you are most apt to play the</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.188>sir in. Very good; well kissed! an excellent</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.189>courtesy! 'tis so, indeed. Yet again your fingers</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.190>to your lips? would they were clyster-pipes for your sake!</p>
<p><i>Trumpet within</i></p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.191>The Moor! I know his trumpet.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech63><b>CASSIO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.192>'Tis truly so.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech64><b>DESDEMONA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.193>Let's meet him and receive him.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech65><b>CASSIO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.194>Lo, where he comes!</p>
<p><i>Enter OTHELLO and Attendants</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech66><b>OTHELLO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.195>O my fair warrior!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech67><b>DESDEMONA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.196>                  My dear Othello!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech68><b>OTHELLO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.197>It gives me wonder great as my content</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.198>To see you here before me. O my soul's joy!</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.199>If after every tempest come such calms,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.200>May the winds blow till they have waken'd death!</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.201>And let the labouring bark climb hills of seas</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.202>Olympus-high and duck again as low</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.203>As hell's from heaven! If it were now to die,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.204>'Twere now to be most happy; for, I fear,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.205>My soul hath her content so absolute</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.206>That not another comfort like to this</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.207>Succeeds in unknown fate.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech69><b>DESDEMONA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.208>The heavens forbid</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.209>But that our loves and comforts should increase,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.210>Even as our days do grow!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech70><b>OTHELLO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.211>Amen to that, sweet powers!</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.212>I cannot speak enough of this content;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.213>It stops me here; it is too much of joy:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.214>And this, and this, the greatest discords be</p>
<p><i>Kissing her</i></p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.215>That e'er our hearts shall make!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech71><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.216>[Aside]  O, you are well tuned now!</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.217>But I'll set down the pegs that make this music,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.218>As honest as I am.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech72><b>OTHELLO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.219>                  Come, let us to the castle.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.220>News, friends; our wars are done, the Turks</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.221>are drown'd.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.222>How does my old acquaintance of this isle?</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.223>Honey, you shall be well desired in Cyprus;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.224>I have found great love amongst them. O my sweet,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.225>I prattle out of fashion, and I dote</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.226>In mine own comforts. I prithee, good Iago,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.227>Go to the bay and disembark my coffers:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.228>Bring thou the master to the citadel;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.229>He is a good one, and his worthiness</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.230>Does challenge much respect. Come, Desdemona,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.231>Once more, well met at Cyprus.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt OTHELLO, DESDEMONA, and Attendants</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech73><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.232>Do thou meet me presently at the harbour. Come</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.233>hither. If thou be'st valiant,-- as, they say, base</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.234>men being in love have then a nobility in their</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.235>natures more than is native to them--list me. The</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.236>lieutenant tonight watches on the court of</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.237>guard:--first, I must tell thee this--Desdemona is</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.238>directly in love with him.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech74><b>RODERIGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.239>With him! why, 'tis not possible.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech75><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.240>Lay thy finger thus, and let thy soul be instructed.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.241>Mark me with what violence she first loved the Moor,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.242>but for bragging and telling her fantastical lies:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.243>and will she love him still for prating? let not</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.244>thy discreet heart think it. Her eye must be fed;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.245>and what delight shall she have to look on the</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.246>devil? When the blood is made dull with the act of</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.247>sport, there should be, again to inflame it and to</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.248>give satiety a fresh appetite, loveliness in favour,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.249>sympathy in years, manners and beauties; all which</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.250>the Moor is defective in: now, for want of these</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.251>required conveniences, her delicate tenderness will</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.252>find itself abused, begin to heave the gorge,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.253>disrelish and abhor the Moor; very nature will</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.254>instruct her in it and compel her to some second</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.255>choice. Now, sir, this granted,--as it is a most</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.256>pregnant and unforced position--who stands so</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.257>eminent in the degree of this fortune as Cassio</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.258>does? a knave very voluble; no further</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.259>conscionable than in putting on the mere form of</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.260>civil and humane seeming, for the better compassing</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.261>of his salt and most hidden loose affection? why,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.262>none; why, none: a slipper and subtle knave, a</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.263>finder of occasions, that has an eye can stamp and</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.264>counterfeit advantages, though true advantage never</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.265>present itself; a devilish knave. Besides, the</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.266>knave is handsome, young, and hath all those</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.267>requisites in him that folly and green minds look</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.268>after: a pestilent complete knave; and the woman</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.269>hath found him already.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech76><b>RODERIGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.270>I cannot believe that in her; she's full of</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.271>most blessed condition.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech77><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.272>Blessed fig's-end! the wine she drinks is made of</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.273>grapes: if she had been blessed, she would never</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.274>have loved the Moor. Blessed pudding! Didst thou</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.275>not see her paddle with the palm of his hand? didst</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.276>not mark that?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech78><b>RODERIGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.277>Yes, that I did; but that was but courtesy.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech79><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.278>Lechery, by this hand; an index and obscure prologue</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.279>to the history of lust and foul thoughts. They met</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.280>so near with their lips that their breaths embraced</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.281>together. Villanous thoughts, Roderigo! when these</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.282>mutualities so marshal the way, hard at hand comes</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.283>the master and main exercise, the incorporate</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.284>conclusion, Pish! But, sir, be you ruled by me: I</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.285>have brought you from Venice. Watch you to-night;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.286>for the command, I'll lay't upon you. Cassio knows</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.287>you not. I'll not be far from you: do you find</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.288>some occasion to anger Cassio, either by speaking</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.289>too loud, or tainting his discipline; or from what</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.290>other course you please, which the time shall more</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.291>favourably minister.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech80><b>RODERIGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.292>Well.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech81><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.293>Sir, he is rash and very sudden in choler, and haply</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.294>may strike at you: provoke him, that he may; for</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.295>even out of that will I cause these of Cyprus to</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.296>mutiny; whose qualification shall come into no true</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.297>taste again but by the displanting of Cassio. So</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.298>shall you have a shorter journey to your desires by</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.299>the means I shall then have to prefer them; and the</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.300>impediment most profitably removed, without the</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.301>which there were no expectation of our prosperity.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech82><b>RODERIGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.302>I will do this, if I can bring it to any</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.303>opportunity.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech83><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.304>I warrant thee. Meet me by and by at the citadel:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.305>I must fetch his necessaries ashore. Farewell.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech84><b>RODERIGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.306>Adieu.</p>
<p><i>Exit</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech85><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.1.307>That Cassio loves her, I do well believe it;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.308>That she loves him, 'tis apt and of great credit:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.309>The Moor, howbeit that I endure him not,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.310>Is of a constant, loving, noble nature,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.311>And I dare think he'll prove to Desdemona</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.312>A most dear husband. Now, I do love her too;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.313>Not out of absolute lust, though peradventure</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.314>I stand accountant for as great a sin,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.315>But partly led to diet my revenge,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.316>For that I do suspect the lusty Moor</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.317>Hath leap'd into my seat; the thought whereof</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.318>Doth, like a poisonous mineral, gnaw my inwards;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.319>And nothing can or shall content my soul</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.320>Till I am even'd with him, wife for wife,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.321>Or failing so, yet that I put the Moor</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.322>At least into a jealousy so strong</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.323>That judgment cannot cure. Which thing to do,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.324>If this poor trash of Venice, whom I trash</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.325>For his quick hunting, stand the putting on,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.326>I'll have our Michael Cassio on the hip,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.327>Abuse him to the Moor in the rank garb--</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.328>For I fear Cassio with my night-cap too--</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.329>Make the Moor thank me, love me and reward me.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.330>For making him egregiously an ass</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.331>And practising upon his peace and quiet</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.332>Even to madness. 'Tis here, but yet confused:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.1.333>Knavery's plain face is never seen tin used.</p>
<p><i>Exit</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE II. A street.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Enter a Herald with a proclamation; People following</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>Herald</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.2.1>It is Othello's pleasure, our noble and valiant</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.2>general, that, upon certain tidings now arrived,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.3>importing the mere perdition of the Turkish fleet,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.4>every man put himself into triumph; some to dance,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.5>some to make bonfires, each man to what sport and</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.6>revels his addiction leads him: for, besides these</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.7>beneficial news, it is the celebration of his</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.8>nuptial. So much was his pleasure should be</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.9>proclaimed. All offices are open, and there is full</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.10>liberty of feasting from this present hour of five</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.11>till the bell have told eleven. Heaven bless the</p>
<p class="line" name=2.2.12>isle of Cyprus and our noble general Othello!</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE III. A hall in the castle.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Enter OTHELLO, DESDEMONA, CASSIO, and Attendants</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>OTHELLO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.1>Good Michael, look you to the guard to-night:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.2>Let's teach ourselves that honourable stop,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.3>Not to outsport discretion.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>CASSIO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.4>Iago hath direction what to do;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.5>But, notwithstanding, with my personal eye</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.6>Will I look to't.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>OTHELLO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.7>                  Iago is most honest.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.8>Michael, good night: to-morrow with your earliest</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.9>Let me have speech with you.</p>
<p><i>To DESDEMONA</i></p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.10>Come, my dear love,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.11>The purchase made, the fruits are to ensue;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.12>That profit's yet to come 'tween me and you.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.13>Good night.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt OTHELLO, DESDEMONA, and Attendants</i></p>
<p><i>Enter IAGO</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>CASSIO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.14>Welcome, Iago; we must to the watch.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.15>Not this hour, lieutenant; 'tis not yet ten o' the</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.16>clock. Our general cast us thus early for the love</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.17>of his Desdemona; who let us not therefore blame:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.18>he hath not yet made wanton the night with her; and</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.19>she is sport for Jove.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>CASSIO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.20>She's a most exquisite lady.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.21>And, I'll warrant her, fun of game.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>CASSIO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.22>Indeed, she's a most fresh and delicate creature.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech9><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.23>What an eye she has! methinks it sounds a parley of</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.24>provocation.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech10><b>CASSIO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.25>An inviting eye; and yet methinks right modest.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech11><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.26>And when she speaks, is it not an alarum to love?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech12><b>CASSIO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.27>She is indeed perfection.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech13><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.28>Well, happiness to their sheets! Come, lieutenant, I</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.29>have a stoup of wine; and here without are a brace</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.30>of Cyprus gallants that would fain have a measure to</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.31>the health of black Othello.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech14><b>CASSIO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.32>Not to-night, good Iago: I have very poor and</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.33>unhappy brains for drinking: I could well wish</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.34>courtesy would invent some other custom of</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.35>entertainment.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech15><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.36>O, they are our friends; but one cup: I'll drink for</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.37>you.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech16><b>CASSIO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.38>I have drunk but one cup to-night, and that was</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.39>craftily qualified too, and, behold, what innovation</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.40>it makes here: I am unfortunate in the infirmity,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.41>and dare not task my weakness with any more.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech17><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.42>What, man! 'tis a night of revels: the gallants</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.43>desire it.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech18><b>CASSIO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.44>Where are they?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech19><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.45>Here at the door; I pray you, call them in.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech20><b>CASSIO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.46>I'll do't; but it dislikes me.</p>
<p><i>Exit</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech21><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.47>If I can fasten but one cup upon him,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.48>With that which he hath drunk to-night already,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.49>He'll be as full of quarrel and offence</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.50>As my young mistress' dog. Now, my sick fool Roderigo,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.51>Whom love hath turn'd almost the wrong side out,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.52>To Desdemona hath to-night caroused</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.53>Potations pottle-deep; and he's to watch:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.54>Three lads of Cyprus, noble swelling spirits,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.55>That hold their honours in a wary distance,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.56>The very elements of this warlike isle,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.57>Have I to-night fluster'd with flowing cups,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.58>And they watch too. Now, 'mongst this flock of drunkards,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.59>Am I to put our Cassio in some action</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.60>That may offend the isle.--But here they come:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.61>If consequence do but approve my dream,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.62>My boat sails freely, both with wind and stream.</p>
<p><i>Re-enter CASSIO; with him MONTANO and Gentlemen; servants following with wine</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech22><b>CASSIO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.63>'Fore God, they have given me a rouse already.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech23><b>MONTANO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.64>Good faith, a little one; not past a pint, as I am</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.65>a soldier.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech24><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.66>Some wine, ho!</p>
<p><i>Sings</i></p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.67>And let me the canakin clink, clink;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.68>And let me the canakin clink</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.69>A soldier's a man;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.70>A life's but a span;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.71>Why, then, let a soldier drink.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.72>Some wine, boys!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech25><b>CASSIO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.73>'Fore God, an excellent song.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech26><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.74>I learned it in England, where, indeed, they are</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.75>most potent in potting: your Dane, your German, and</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.76>your swag-bellied Hollander--Drink, ho!--are nothing</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.77>to your English.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech27><b>CASSIO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.78>Is your Englishman so expert in his drinking?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech28><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.79>Why, he drinks you, with facility, your Dane dead</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.80>drunk; he sweats not to overthrow your Almain; he</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.81>gives your Hollander a vomit, ere the next pottle</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.82>can be filled.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech29><b>CASSIO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.83>To the health of our general!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech30><b>MONTANO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.84>I am for it, lieutenant; and I'll do you justice.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech31><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.85>O sweet England!</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.86>King Stephen was a worthy peer,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.87>His breeches cost him but a crown;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.88>He held them sixpence all too dear,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.89>With that he call'd the tailor lown.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.90>He was a wight of high renown,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.91>And thou art but of low degree:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.92>'Tis pride that pulls the country down;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.93>Then take thine auld cloak about thee.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.94>Some wine, ho!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech32><b>CASSIO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.95>Why, this is a more exquisite song than the other.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech33><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.96>Will you hear't again?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech34><b>CASSIO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.97>No; for I hold him to be unworthy of his place that</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.98>does those things. Well, God's above all; and there</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.99>be souls must be saved, and there be souls must not be saved.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech35><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.100>It's true, good lieutenant.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech36><b>CASSIO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.101>For mine own part,--no offence to the general, nor</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.102>any man of quality,--I hope to be saved.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech37><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.103>And so do I too, lieutenant.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech38><b>CASSIO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.104>Ay, but, by your leave, not before me; the</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.105>lieutenant is to be saved before the ancient. Let's</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.106>have no more of this; let's to our affairs.--Forgive</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.107>us our sins!--Gentlemen, let's look to our business.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.108>Do not think, gentlemen. I am drunk: this is my</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.109>ancient; this is my right hand, and this is my left:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.110>I am not drunk now; I can stand well enough, and</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.111>speak well enough.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech39><b>All</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.112>Excellent well.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech40><b>CASSIO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.113>Why, very well then; you must not think then that I am drunk.</p>
<p><i>Exit</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech41><b>MONTANO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.114>To the platform, masters; come, let's set the watch.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech42><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.115>You see this fellow that is gone before;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.116>He is a soldier fit to stand by Caesar</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.117>And give direction: and do but see his vice;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.118>'Tis to his virtue a just equinox,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.119>The one as long as the other: 'tis pity of him.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.120>I fear the trust Othello puts him in.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.121>On some odd time of his infirmity,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.122>Will shake this island.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech43><b>MONTANO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.123>But is he often thus?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech44><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.124>'Tis evermore the prologue to his sleep:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.125>He'll watch the horologe a double set,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.126>If drink rock not his cradle.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech45><b>MONTANO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.127>It were well</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.128>The general were put in mind of it.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.129>Perhaps he sees it not; or his good nature</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.130>Prizes the virtue that appears in Cassio,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.131>And looks not on his evils: is not this true?</p>
<p><i>Enter RODERIGO</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech46><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.132>[Aside to him]  How now, Roderigo!</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.133>I pray you, after the lieutenant; go.</p>
<p><i>Exit RODERIGO</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech47><b>MONTANO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.134>And 'tis great pity that the noble Moor</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.135>Should hazard such a place as his own second</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.136>With one of an ingraft infirmity:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.137>It were an honest action to say</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.138>So to the Moor.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech48><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.139>                  Not I, for this fair island:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.140>I do love Cassio well; and would do much</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.141>To cure him of this evil--But, hark! what noise?</p>
<p><i>Cry within: 'Help! help!'</i></p>
<p><i>Re-enter CASSIO, driving in RODERIGO</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech49><b>CASSIO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.142>You rogue! you rascal!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech50><b>MONTANO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.143>What's the matter, lieutenant?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech51><b>CASSIO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.144>A knave teach me my duty!</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.145>I'll beat the knave into a twiggen bottle.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech52><b>RODERIGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.146>Beat me!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech53><b>CASSIO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.147>       Dost thou prate, rogue?</p>
<p><i>Striking RODERIGO</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech54><b>MONTANO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.148>Nay, good lieutenant;</p>
<p><i>Staying him</i></p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.149>I pray you, sir, hold your hand.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech55><b>CASSIO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.150>Let me go, sir,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.151>Or I'll knock you o'er the mazzard.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech56><b>MONTANO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.152>Come, come,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.153>you're drunk.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech57><b>CASSIO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.154>Drunk!</p>
<p><i>They fight</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech58><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.155>[Aside to RODERIGO]  Away, I say; go out, and cry a mutiny.</p>
<p><i>Exit RODERIGO</i></p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.156>Nay, good lieutenant,--alas, gentlemen;--</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.157>Help, ho!--Lieutenant,--sir,--Montano,--sir;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.158>Help, masters!--Here's a goodly watch indeed!</p>
<p><i>Bell rings</i></p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.159>Who's that which rings the bell?--Diablo, ho!</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.160>The town will rise: God's will, lieutenant, hold!</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.161>You will be shamed for ever.</p>
<p><i>Re-enter OTHELLO and Attendants</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech59><b>OTHELLO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.162>What is the matter here?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech60><b>MONTANO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.163>'Zounds, I bleed still; I am hurt to the death.</p>
<p><i>Faints</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech61><b>OTHELLO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.164>Hold, for your lives!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech62><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.165>Hold, ho! Lieutenant,--sir--Montano,--gentlemen,--</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.166>Have you forgot all sense of place and duty?</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.167>Hold! the general speaks to you; hold, hold, for shame!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech63><b>OTHELLO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.168>Why, how now, ho! from whence ariseth this?</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.169>Are we turn'd Turks, and to ourselves do that</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.170>Which heaven hath forbid the Ottomites?</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.171>For Christian shame, put by this barbarous brawl:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.172>He that stirs next to carve for his own rage</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.173>Holds his soul light; he dies upon his motion.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.174>Silence that dreadful bell: it frights the isle</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.175>From her propriety. What is the matter, masters?</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.176>Honest Iago, that look'st dead with grieving,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.177>Speak, who began this? on thy love, I charge thee.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech64><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.178>I do not know: friends all but now, even now,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.179>In quarter, and in terms like bride and groom</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.180>Devesting them for bed; and then, but now--</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.181>As if some planet had unwitted men--</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.182>Swords out, and tilting one at other's breast,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.183>In opposition bloody. I cannot speak</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.184>Any beginning to this peevish odds;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.185>And would in action glorious I had lost</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.186>Those legs that brought me to a part of it!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech65><b>OTHELLO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.187>How comes it, Michael, you are thus forgot?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech66><b>CASSIO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.188>I pray you, pardon me; I cannot speak.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech67><b>OTHELLO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.189>Worthy Montano, you were wont be civil;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.190>The gravity and stillness of your youth</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.191>The world hath noted, and your name is great</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.192>In mouths of wisest censure: what's the matter,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.193>That you unlace your reputation thus</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.194>And spend your rich opinion for the name</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.195>Of a night-brawler? give me answer to it.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech68><b>MONTANO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.196>Worthy Othello, I am hurt to danger:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.197>Your officer, Iago, can inform you,--</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.198>While I spare speech, which something now</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.199>offends me,--</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.200>Of all that I do know: nor know I aught</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.201>By me that's said or done amiss this night;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.202>Unless self-charity be sometimes a vice,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.203>And to defend ourselves it be a sin</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.204>When violence assails us.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech69><b>OTHELLO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.205>Now, by heaven,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.206>My blood begins my safer guides to rule;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.207>And passion, having my best judgment collied,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.208>Assays to lead the way: if I once stir,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.209>Or do but lift this arm, the best of you</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.210>Shall sink in my rebuke. Give me to know</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.211>How this foul rout began, who set it on;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.212>And he that is approved in this offence,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.213>Though he had twinn'd with me, both at a birth,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.214>Shall lose me. What! in a town of war,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.215>Yet wild, the people's hearts brimful of fear,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.216>To manage private and domestic quarrel,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.217>In night, and on the court and guard of safety!</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.218>'Tis monstrous. Iago, who began't?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech70><b>MONTANO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.219>If partially affined, or leagued in office,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.220>Thou dost deliver more or less than truth,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.221>Thou art no soldier.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech71><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.222>Touch me not so near:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.223>I had rather have this tongue cut from my mouth</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.224>Than it should do offence to Michael Cassio;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.225>Yet, I persuade myself, to speak the truth</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.226>Shall nothing wrong him. Thus it is, general.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.227>Montano and myself being in speech,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.228>There comes a fellow crying out for help:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.229>And Cassio following him with determined sword,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.230>To execute upon him. Sir, this gentleman</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.231>Steps in to Cassio, and entreats his pause:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.232>Myself the crying fellow did pursue,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.233>Lest by his clamour--as it so fell out--</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.234>The town might fall in fright: he, swift of foot,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.235>Outran my purpose; and I return'd the rather</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.236>For that I heard the clink and fall of swords,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.237>And Cassio high in oath; which till to-night</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.238>I ne'er might say before. When I came back--</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.239>For this was brief--I found them close together,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.240>At blow and thrust; even as again they were</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.241>When you yourself did part them.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.242>More of this matter cannot I report:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.243>But men are men; the best sometimes forget:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.244>Though Cassio did some little wrong to him,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.245>As men in rage strike those that wish them best,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.246>Yet surely Cassio, I believe, received</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.247>From him that fled some strange indignity,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.248>Which patience could not pass.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech72><b>OTHELLO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.249>I know, Iago,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.250>Thy honesty and love doth mince this matter,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.251>Making it light to Cassio. Cassio, I love thee</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.252>But never more be officer of mine.</p>
<p><i>Re-enter DESDEMONA, attended</i></p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.253>Look, if my gentle love be not raised up!</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.254>I'll make thee an example.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech73><b>DESDEMONA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.255>What's the matter?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech74><b>OTHELLO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.256>All's well now, sweeting; come away to bed.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.257>Sir, for your hurts, myself will be your surgeon:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.258>Lead him off.</p>
<p><i>To MONTANO, who is led off</i></p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.259>Iago, look with care about the town,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.260>And silence those whom this vile brawl distracted.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.261>Come, Desdemona: 'tis the soldiers' life</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.262>To have their balmy slumbers waked with strife.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt all but IAGO and CASSIO</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech75><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.263>What, are you hurt, lieutenant?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech76><b>CASSIO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.264>Ay, past all surgery.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech77><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.265>Marry, heaven forbid!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech78><b>CASSIO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.266>Reputation, reputation, reputation! O, I have lost</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.267>my reputation! I have lost the immortal part of</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.268>myself, and what remains is bestial. My reputation,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.269>Iago, my reputation!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech79><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.270>As I am an honest man, I thought you had received</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.271>some bodily wound; there is more sense in that than</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.272>in reputation. Reputation is an idle and most false</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.273>imposition: oft got without merit, and lost without</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.274>deserving: you have lost no reputation at all,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.275>unless you repute yourself such a loser. What, man!</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.276>there are ways to recover the general again: you</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.277>are but now cast in his mood, a punishment more in</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.278>policy than in malice, even so as one would beat his</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.279>offenceless dog to affright an imperious lion: sue</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.280>to him again, and he's yours.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech80><b>CASSIO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.281>I will rather sue to be despised than to deceive so</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.282>good a commander with so slight, so drunken, and so</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.283>indiscreet an officer. Drunk? and speak parrot?</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.284>and squabble? swagger? swear? and discourse</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.285>fustian with one's own shadow? O thou invisible</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.286>spirit of wine, if thou hast no name to be known by,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.287>let us call thee devil!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech81><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.288>What was he that you followed with your sword? What</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.289>had he done to you?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech82><b>CASSIO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.290>I know not.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech83><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.291>Is't possible?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech84><b>CASSIO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.292>I remember a mass of things, but nothing distinctly;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.293>a quarrel, but nothing wherefore. O God, that men</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.294>should put an enemy in their mouths to steal away</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.295>their brains! that we should, with joy, pleasance</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.296>revel and applause, transform ourselves into beasts!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech85><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.297>Why, but you are now well enough: how came you thus</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.298>recovered?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech86><b>CASSIO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.299>It hath pleased the devil drunkenness to give place</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.300>to the devil wrath; one unperfectness shows me</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.301>another, to make me frankly despise myself.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech87><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.302>Come, you are too severe a moraler: as the time,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.303>the place, and the condition of this country</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.304>stands, I could heartily wish this had not befallen;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.305>but, since it is as it is, mend it for your own good.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech88><b>CASSIO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.306>I will ask him for my place again; he shall tell me</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.307>I am a drunkard! Had I as many mouths as Hydra,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.308>such an answer would stop them all. To be now a</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.309>sensible man, by and by a fool, and presently a</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.310>beast! O strange! Every inordinate cup is</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.311>unblessed and the ingredient is a devil.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech89><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.312>Come, come, good wine is a good familiar creature,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.313>if it be well used: exclaim no more against it.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.314>And, good lieutenant, I think you think I love you.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech90><b>CASSIO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.315>I have well approved it, sir. I drunk!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech91><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.316>You or any man living may be drunk! at a time, man.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.317>I'll tell you what you shall do. Our general's wife</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.318>is now the general: may say so in this respect, for</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.319>that he hath devoted and given up himself to the</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.320>contemplation, mark, and denotement of her parts and</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.321>graces: confess yourself freely to her; importune</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.322>her help to put you in your place again: she is of</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.323>so free, so kind, so apt, so blessed a disposition,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.324>she holds it a vice in her goodness not to do more</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.325>than she is requested: this broken joint between</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.326>you and her husband entreat her to splinter; and, my</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.327>fortunes against any lay worth naming, this</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.328>crack of your love shall grow stronger than it was before.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech92><b>CASSIO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.329>You advise me well.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech93><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.330>I protest, in the sincerity of love and honest kindness.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech94><b>CASSIO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.331>I think it freely; and betimes in the morning I will</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.332>beseech the virtuous Desdemona to undertake for me:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.333>I am desperate of my fortunes if they cheque me here.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech95><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.334>You are in the right. Good night, lieutenant; I</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.335>must to the watch.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.336>CASSIO: Good night, honest Iago.</p>
<p><i>Exit</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech96><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.337>And what's he then that says I play the villain?</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.338>When this advice is free I give and honest,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.339>Probal to thinking and indeed the course</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.340>To win the Moor again? For 'tis most easy</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.341>The inclining Desdemona to subdue</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.342>In any honest suit: she's framed as fruitful</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.343>As the free elements. And then for her</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.344>To win the Moor--were't to renounce his baptism,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.345>All seals and symbols of redeemed sin,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.346>His soul is so enfetter'd to her love,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.347>That she may make, unmake, do what she list,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.348>Even as her appetite shall play the god</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.349>With his weak function. How am I then a villain</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.350>To counsel Cassio to this parallel course,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.351>Directly to his good? Divinity of hell!</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.352>When devils will the blackest sins put on,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.353>They do suggest at first with heavenly shows,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.354>As I do now: for whiles this honest fool</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.355>Plies Desdemona to repair his fortunes</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.356>And she for him pleads strongly to the Moor,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.357>I'll pour this pestilence into his ear,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.358>That she repeals him for her body's lust;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.359>And by how much she strives to do him good,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.360>She shall undo her credit with the Moor.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.361>So will I turn her virtue into pitch,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.362>And out of her own goodness make the net</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.363>That shall enmesh them all.</p>
<p><i>Re-enter RODERIGO</i></p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.364>How now, Roderigo!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech97><b>RODERIGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.365>I do follow here in the chase, not like a hound that</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.366>hunts, but one that fills up the cry. My money is</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.367>almost spent; I have been to-night exceedingly well</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.368>cudgelled; and I think the issue will be, I shall</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.369>have so much experience for my pains, and so, with</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.370>no money at all and a little more wit, return again to Venice.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech98><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=2.3.371>How poor are they that have not patience!</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.372>What wound did ever heal but by degrees?</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.373>Thou know'st we work by wit, and not by witchcraft;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.374>And wit depends on dilatory time.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.375>Does't not go well? Cassio hath beaten thee.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.376>And thou, by that small hurt, hast cashier'd Cassio:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.377>Though other things grow fair against the sun,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.378>Yet fruits that blossom first will first be ripe:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.379>Content thyself awhile. By the mass, 'tis morning;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.380>Pleasure and action make the hours seem short.</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.381>Retire thee; go where thou art billeted:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.382>Away, I say; thou shalt know more hereafter:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.383>Nay, get thee gone.</p>
<p><i>Exit RODERIGO</i></p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.384>Two things are to be done:</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.385>My wife must move for Cassio to her mistress;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.386>I'll set her on;</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.387>Myself the while to draw the Moor apart,</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.388>And bring him jump when he may Cassio find</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.389>Soliciting his wife: ay, that's the way</p>
<p class="line" name=2.3.390>Dull not device by coldness and delay.</p>
<p><i>Exit</i></p>
</blockquote><p>
<H3>ACT III</h3>
<h3>SCENE I. Before the castle.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Enter CASSIO and some Musicians</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>CASSIO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.1>Masters, play here; I will content your pains;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.2>Something that's brief; and bid 'Good morrow, general.'</p>
<p><i>Music</i></p>
<p><i>Enter Clown</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>Clown</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.3>Why masters, have your instruments been in Naples,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.4>that they speak i' the nose thus?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>First Musician</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.5>How, sir, how!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>Clown</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.6>Are these, I pray you, wind-instruments?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>First Musician</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.7>Ay, marry, are they, sir.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>Clown</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.8>O, thereby hangs a tail.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>First Musician</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.9>Whereby hangs a tale, sir?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>Clown</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.10>Marry. sir, by many a wind-instrument that I know.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.11>But, masters, here's money for you: and the general</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.12>so likes your music, that he desires you, for love's</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.13>sake, to make no more noise with it.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech9><b>First Musician</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.14>Well, sir, we will not.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech10><b>Clown</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.15>If you have any music that may not be heard, to't</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.16>again: but, as they say to hear music the general</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.17>does not greatly care.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech11><b>First Musician</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.18>We have none such, sir.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech12><b>Clown</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.19>Then put up your pipes in your bag, for I'll away:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.20>go; vanish into air; away!</p>
<p><i>Exeunt Musicians</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech13><b>CASSIO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.21>Dost thou hear, my honest friend?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech14><b>Clown</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.22>No, I hear not your honest friend; I hear you.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech15><b>CASSIO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.23>Prithee, keep up thy quillets. There's a poor piece</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.24>of gold for thee: if the gentlewoman that attends</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.25>the general's wife be stirring, tell her there's</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.26>one Cassio entreats her a little favour of speech:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.27>wilt thou do this?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech16><b>Clown</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.28>She is stirring, sir: if she will stir hither, I</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.29>shall seem to notify unto her.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech17><b>CASSIO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.30>Do, good my friend.</p>
<p><i>Exit Clown</i></p>
<p><i>Enter IAGO</i></p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.31>In happy time, Iago.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech18><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.32>You have not been a-bed, then?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech19><b>CASSIO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.33>Why, no; the day had broke</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.34>Before we parted. I have made bold, Iago,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.35>To send in to your wife: my suit to her</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.36>Is, that she will to virtuous Desdemona</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.37>Procure me some access.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech20><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.38>I'll send her to you presently;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.39>And I'll devise a mean to draw the Moor</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.40>Out of the way, that your converse and business</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.41>May be more free.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech21><b>CASSIO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.42>I humbly thank you for't.</p>
<p><i>Exit IAGO</i></p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.43>I never knew</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.44>A Florentine more kind and honest.</p>
<p><i>Enter EMILIA</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech22><b>EMILIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.45>Good morrow, good Lieutenant: I am sorry</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.46>For your displeasure; but all will sure be well.</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.47>The general and his wife are talking of it;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.48>And she speaks for you stoutly: the Moor replies,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.49>That he you hurt is of great fame in Cyprus,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.50>And great affinity, and that in wholesome wisdom</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.51>He might not but refuse you; but he protests he loves you</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.52>And needs no other suitor but his likings</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.53>To take the safest occasion by the front</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.54>To bring you in again.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech23><b>CASSIO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.55>Yet, I beseech you,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.56>If you think fit, or that it may be done,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.57>Give me advantage of some brief discourse</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.58>With Desdemona alone.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech24><b>EMILIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.59>Pray you, come in;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.60>I will bestow you where you shall have time</p>
<p class="line" name=3.1.61>To speak your bosom freely.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech25><b>CASSIO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.1.62>I am much bound to you.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE II. A room in the castle.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Enter OTHELLO, IAGO, and Gentlemen</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>OTHELLO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.1>These letters give, Iago, to the pilot;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.2>And by him do my duties to the senate:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.3>That done, I will be walking on the works;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.2.4>Repair there to me.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.5>Well, my good lord, I'll do't.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>OTHELLO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.6>This fortification, gentlemen, shall we see't?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>Gentleman</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.2.7>We'll wait upon your lordship.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt</i></p>
</blockquote>
<h3>SCENE III. The garden of the castle.</h3>
<p><blockquote>
<i>Enter DESDEMONA, CASSIO, and EMILIA</i>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech1><b>DESDEMONA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.1>Be thou assured, good Cassio, I will do</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.2>All my abilities in thy behalf.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech2><b>EMILIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.3>Good madam, do: I warrant it grieves my husband,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.4>As if the case were his.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech3><b>DESDEMONA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.5>O, that's an honest fellow. Do not doubt, Cassio,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.6>But I will have my lord and you again</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.7>As friendly as you were.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech4><b>CASSIO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.8>Bounteous madam,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.9>Whatever shall become of Michael Cassio,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.10>He's never any thing but your true servant.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech5><b>DESDEMONA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.11>I know't; I thank you. You do love my lord:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.12>You have known him long; and be you well assured</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.13>He shall in strangeness stand no further off</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.14>Than in a polite distance.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech6><b>CASSIO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.15>Ay, but, lady,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.16>That policy may either last so long,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.17>Or feed upon such nice and waterish diet,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.18>Or breed itself so out of circumstance,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.19>That, I being absent and my place supplied,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.20>My general will forget my love and service.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech7><b>DESDEMONA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.21>Do not doubt that; before Emilia here</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.22>I give thee warrant of thy place: assure thee,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.23>If I do vow a friendship, I'll perform it</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.24>To the last article: my lord shall never rest;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.25>I'll watch him tame and talk him out of patience;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.26>His bed shall seem a school, his board a shrift;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.27>I'll intermingle every thing he does</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.28>With Cassio's suit: therefore be merry, Cassio;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.29>For thy solicitor shall rather die</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.30>Than give thy cause away.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech8><b>EMILIA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.31>Madam, here comes my lord.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech9><b>CASSIO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.32>Madam, I'll take my leave.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech10><b>DESDEMONA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.33>Why, stay, and hear me speak.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech11><b>CASSIO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.34>Madam, not now: I am very ill at ease,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.35>Unfit for mine own purposes.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech12><b>DESDEMONA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.36>Well, do your discretion.</p>
<p><i>Exit CASSIO</i></p>
<p><i>Enter OTHELLO and IAGO</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech13><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.37>Ha! I like not that.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech14><b>OTHELLO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.38>What dost thou say?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech15><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.39>Nothing, my lord: or if--I know not what.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech16><b>OTHELLO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.40>Was not that Cassio parted from my wife?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech17><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.41>Cassio, my lord! No, sure, I cannot think it,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.42>That he would steal away so guilty-like,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.43>Seeing you coming.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech18><b>OTHELLO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.44>                  I do believe 'twas he.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech19><b>DESDEMONA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.45>How now, my lord!</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.46>I have been talking with a suitor here,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.47>A man that languishes in your displeasure.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech20><b>OTHELLO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.48>Who is't you mean?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech21><b>DESDEMONA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.49>Why, your lieutenant, Cassio. Good my lord,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.50>If I have any grace or power to move you,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.51>His present reconciliation take;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.52>For if he be not one that truly loves you,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.53>That errs in ignorance and not in cunning,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.54>I have no judgment in an honest face:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.55>I prithee, call him back.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech22><b>OTHELLO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.56>Went he hence now?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech23><b>DESDEMONA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.57>Ay, sooth; so humbled</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.58>That he hath left part of his grief with me,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.59>To suffer with him. Good love, call him back.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech24><b>OTHELLO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.60>Not now, sweet Desdemona; some other time.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech25><b>DESDEMONA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.61>But shall't be shortly?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech26><b>OTHELLO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.62>The sooner, sweet, for you.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech27><b>DESDEMONA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.63>Shall't be to-night at supper?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech28><b>OTHELLO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.64>No, not to-night.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech29><b>DESDEMONA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.65>To-morrow dinner, then?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech30><b>OTHELLO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.66>I shall not dine at home;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.67>I meet the captains at the citadel.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech31><b>DESDEMONA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.68>Why, then, to-morrow night; or Tuesday morn;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.69>On Tuesday noon, or night; on Wednesday morn:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.70>I prithee, name the time, but let it not</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.71>Exceed three days: in faith, he's penitent;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.72>And yet his trespass, in our common reason--</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.73>Save that, they say, the wars must make examples</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.74>Out of their best--is not almost a fault</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.75>To incur a private cheque. When shall he come?</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.76>Tell me, Othello: I wonder in my soul,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.77>What you would ask me, that I should deny,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.78>Or stand so mammering on. What! Michael Cassio,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.79>That came a-wooing with you, and so many a time,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.80>When I have spoke of you dispraisingly,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.81>Hath ta'en your part; to have so much to do</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.82>To bring him in! Trust me, I could do much,--</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech32><b>OTHELLO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.83>Prithee, no more: let him come when he will;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.84>I will deny thee nothing.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech33><b>DESDEMONA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.85>Why, this is not a boon;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.86>'Tis as I should entreat you wear your gloves,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.87>Or feed on nourishing dishes, or keep you warm,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.88>Or sue to you to do a peculiar profit</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.89>To your own person: nay, when I have a suit</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.90>Wherein I mean to touch your love indeed,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.91>It shall be full of poise and difficult weight</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.92>And fearful to be granted.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech34><b>OTHELLO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.93>I will deny thee nothing:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.94>Whereon, I do beseech thee, grant me this,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.95>To leave me but a little to myself.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech35><b>DESDEMONA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.96>Shall I deny you? no: farewell, my lord.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech36><b>OTHELLO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.97>Farewell, my Desdemona: I'll come to thee straight.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech37><b>DESDEMONA</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.98>Emilia, come. Be as your fancies teach you;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.99>Whate'er you be, I am obedient.</p>
<p><i>Exeunt DESDEMONA and EMILIA</i></p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech38><b>OTHELLO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.100>Excellent wretch! Perdition catch my soul,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.101>But I do love thee! and when I love thee not,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.102>Chaos is come again.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech39><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.103>My noble lord--</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech40><b>OTHELLO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.104>                  What dost thou say, Iago?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech41><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.105>Did Michael Cassio, when you woo'd my lady,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.106>Know of your love?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech42><b>OTHELLO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.107>He did, from first to last: why dost thou ask?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech43><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.108>But for a satisfaction of my thought;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.109>No further harm.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech44><b>OTHELLO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.110>                  Why of thy thought, Iago?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech45><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.111>I did not think he had been acquainted with her.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech46><b>OTHELLO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.112>O, yes; and went between us very oft.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech47><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.113>Indeed!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech48><b>OTHELLO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.114>Indeed! ay, indeed: discern'st thou aught in that?</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.115>Is he not honest?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech49><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.116>Honest, my lord!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech50><b>OTHELLO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.117>                  Honest! ay, honest.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech51><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.118>My lord, for aught I know.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech52><b>OTHELLO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.119>What dost thou think?</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech53><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.120>Think, my lord!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech54><b>OTHELLO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.121>Think, my lord!</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.122>By heaven, he echoes me,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.123>As if there were some monster in his thought</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.124>Too hideous to be shown. Thou dost mean something:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.125>I heard thee say even now, thou likedst not that,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.126>When Cassio left my wife: what didst not like?</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.127>And when I told thee he was of my counsel</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.128>In my whole course of wooing, thou criedst 'Indeed!'</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.129>And didst contract and purse thy brow together,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.130>As if thou then hadst shut up in thy brain</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.131>Some horrible conceit: if thou dost love me,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.132>Show me thy thought.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech55><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.133>My lord, you know I love you.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech56><b>OTHELLO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.134>I think thou dost;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.135>And, for I know thou'rt full of love and honesty,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.136>And weigh'st thy words before thou givest them breath,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.137>Therefore these stops of thine fright me the more:</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.138>For such things in a false disloyal knave</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.139>Are tricks of custom, but in a man that's just</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.140>They are close delations, working from the heart</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.141>That passion cannot rule.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech57><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.142>For Michael Cassio,</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.143>I dare be sworn I think that he is honest.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech58><b>OTHELLO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.144>I think so too.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech59><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.145>                  Men should be what they seem;</p>
<p class="line" name=3.3.146>Or those that be not, would they might seem none!</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech60><b>OTHELLO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.147>Certain, men should be what they seem.</p>
</blockquote>

<p class="line" name=speech61><b>IAGO</b></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="line" name=3.3.148>Why, then, I think Cassio's an honest man.</p>
</blockquote>
